# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`
- [ ] Provide reasoning for the localization

    10→  "confidence": 0.85,
    11→  "reasoning": "The bug is caused by incomplete signal handling in the NFS inode revalidation path. NFSv3 (nfs3proc.c) has a wrapper function (nfs3_rpc_wrapper) that checks for fatal signals and retries RPC calls when interrupted, but NFSv2 (proc.c) lacks this protection. When rpc_call_sync in nfs_proc_getattr is interrupted by a signal during RPC wait (with TASK_KILLABLE mode in rpc_wait_bit_killable), it returns -ERESTARTSYS. This error is then treated as a hard failure in __nfs_revalidate_inode, causing the inode cache to be invalidated. For autofs mount points, this cache invalidation triggers unmounting of the entire automounted filesystem, causing the mount to disappear. The root issue is that nfs_proc_getattr does not handle the transient -ERESTARTSYS error gracefully, unlike its NFSv3 counterpart. The fix should either: (1) wrap nfs_proc_getattr's rpc_call_sync calls with error handling similar to nfs3_rpc_wrapper, or (2) modify __nfs_revalidate_inode to retry or handle -ERESTARTSYS specially instead of treating it as a permanent error."
    12→}

80-assistanttext-
## Summary

I've successfully completed the fault localization for the NFS mount disappearance bug. Here are my findings:

### Root Cause

The bug is caused by **incomplete signal handling in the NFS inode revalidation path**:

1. **NFSv3 vs NFSv2 difference**: NFSv3 (in `fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c`) has a wrapper function called `nfs3_rpc_wrapper` that:
   - Checks for fatal signals after RPC calls
   - Retries the RPC call if interrupted by signals
   - Only returns -ERESTARTSYS if a real signal is actually pending

2. **NFSv2 vulnerability**: NFSv2 (`fs/nfs/proc.c`) lacks this protection. When `nfs_proc_getattr` calls `rpc_call_sync` with default flags, the underlying RPC mechanism can be interrupted by signals, returning -ERESTARTSYS.

3. **The cascade**: 
   - Signal interrupts RPC wait (in `rpc_wait_bit_killable` with TASK_KILLABLE mode)
   - `nfs_proc_getattr` returns -ERESTARTSYS error
   - `__nfs_revalidate_inode` treats this as a hard failure (like -ESTALE)
   - Inode cache is invalidated
   - For autofs mount points, this triggers unmounting of the entire automounted filesystem

### Buggy Locations

**Files:**
- `fs/nfs/proc.c` - NFSv2 getattr function
- `fs/nfs/inode.c` - inode revalidation error handling

**Functions:**
- `nfs_proc_getattr()` - Missing error handling for -ERESTARTSYS
- `__nfs_revalidate_inode()` - Treats -ERESTARTSYS as permanent error instead of transient

**Confidence:** 0.85

### Expected Fix

The fix should implement one of:
1. Wrap NFSv2's `rpc_call_sync` calls with error handling similar to `nfs3_rpc_wrapper`
2. Modify `__nfs_revalidate_inode` to detect and retry on -ERESTARTSYS rather than treating it as a permanent error

The result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`.

NFSv3 (nfs3proc.c) has a wrapper function (nfs3_rpc_wrapper) that checks for fatal signals and retries RPC calls when interrupted, but NFSv2 (proc.c) lacks this protection. When rpc_call_sync in nfs_proc_getattr is interrupted by a signal during RPC wait (with TASK_KILLABLE mode in rpc_wait_bit_killable), it returns -ERESTARTSYS. This error is then treated as a hard failure in __nfs_revalidate_inode, causing the inode cache to be invalidated. For autofs mount points, this cache invalidation triggers unmounting of the entire automounted filesystem, causing the mount to disappear. The root issue is that nfs_proc_getattr does not handle the transient -ERESTARTSYS error gracefully, unlike its NFSv3 counterpart. The fix should either: (1) wrap nfs_proc_getattr's rpc_call_sync calls with error handling similar to nfs3_rpc_wrapper, or (2) modify __nfs_revalidate_inode to retry or handle -ERESTARTSYS specially instead of treating it as a permanent error.\"\n}\n",
